<p><b>Roald Engelbregt Gravning Amundsen</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">UK</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/Ë/: primary stress follows">Ë</span><span title="/ÉË/: 'a' in 'father'">ÉË</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/Ê/: 'u' in 'push'">Ê</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/Én/: 'on' in 'button'">Én</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">US</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/É/: 'a' in 'about'">É</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span>-/</a></span></span>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> <small>Norwegian:Â </small><span class="IPA" lang="no-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Norwegian" title="Help:IPA/Norwegian">[ËrÃ¹ËÉÉ« ËÉÌmÊnsÉn]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:RoaldAmundsen.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/90/RoaldAmundsen.ogg" title="RoaldAmundsen.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>; 16 July 1872Â â <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">â18 June 1928</span>) was a <a href="/wiki/Norwegians" title="Norwegians">Norwegian</a> explorer of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polar_region" title="Polar region">polar regions</a>. He was a key figure of the period known as the <a href="/wiki/Heroic_Age_of_Antarctic_Exploration" title="Heroic Age of Antarctic Exploration">Heroic Age of Antarctic Exploration</a>.
</p><p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Borge,_%C3%98stfold" title="Borge, Ãstfold">Borge, Ãstfold</a>, Norway, Amundsen began his career as a polar explorer as first mate on <a href="/wiki/Adrien_de_Gerlache" title="Adrien de Gerlache">Adrien de Gerlache</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Antarctic_Expedition" title="Belgian Antarctic Expedition">Belgian Antarctic Expedition</a> of 1897â1899. From 1903 to 1906, he led the first expedition to successfully traverse the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Passage" title="Northwest Passage">Northwest Passage</a> on the sloop <i><a href="/wiki/Gj%C3%B8a" title="GjÃ¸a">GjÃ¸a</a></i>. In 1909, Amundsen began planning for a <a href="/wiki/Amundsen%27s_South_Pole_expedition" title="Amundsen's South Pole expedition">South Pole expedition</a>. He left Norway in June 1910 on the ship <i><a href="/wiki/Fram_(ship)" title="Fram (ship)">Fram</a></i> and reached <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a> in January 1911. His party established a <a href="/wiki/Framheim" title="Framheim">camp</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Whales" title="Bay of Whales">Bay of Whales</a> and a series of supply depots on the Barrier (now known as the <a href="/wiki/Ross_Ice_Shelf" title="Ross Ice Shelf">Ross Ice Shelf</a>) before setting out for the pole in October. The party of five, led by Amundsen, became the first to successfully <a href="/wiki/Amundsen%27s_South_Pole_expedition" title="Amundsen's South Pole expedition">reach the South Pole</a> on 14 December 1911.
</p><p>Following a failed attempt in 1918 to reach the <a href="/wiki/North_Pole" title="North Pole">North Pole</a> by traversing the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Sea_Route" title="Northern Sea Route">Northeast Passage</a> on the ship <i><a href="/wiki/Maud_(ship)" title="Maud (ship)">Maud</a></i>, Amundsen began planning for an aerial expedition instead. On 12 May 1926, Amundsen and 15 other men in the airship <i><a href="/wiki/Norge_(airship)" title="Norge (airship)">Norge</a></i> became the first explorers verified to have reached the North Pole.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whowasfirstatthenorthpole_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-whowasfirstatthenorthpole-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flyingtothenorthpole_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-flyingtothenorthpole-5">[5]</a></sup> Amundsen disappeared in June 1928 while flying on a rescue mission for the airship <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Airship_Italia" title="Airship Italia"><i>Italia</i></a> in the Arctic. The search for his remains, which have not been found, was called off in September of that year.
</p>

</li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#North_Polar_Expeditions_and_The_Northeast_Passage"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">North Polar Expeditions and The Northeast Passage</span></a>

</ul>
</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roald_Amundsen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Amundsen was born into a family of Norwegian shipowners and captains in <a href="/wiki/Borge,_%C3%98stfold" title="Borge, Ãstfold">Borge</a>, between the towns <a href="/wiki/Fredrikstad" title="Fredrikstad">Fredrikstad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sarpsborg" title="Sarpsborg">Sarpsborg</a>. His parents were Jens Amundsen and Hanna Sahlqvist. Roald was the fourth son in the family. His mother wanted him to avoid the family maritime trade and encouraged him to become a doctor, a promise that Amundsen kept until his mother died when he was aged 21. He promptly quit university for a life at sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thomas_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p><p>When he was fifteen years old, Amundsen was enthralled by reading <a href="/wiki/John_Franklin" title="John Franklin">Sir John Franklin</a>'s narratives of his overland Arctic expeditions. Amundsen wrote "I read them with a fervid fascination which has shaped the whole course of my life".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Life_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Life-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Polar_treks">Polar treks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roald_Amundsen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Polar treks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Belgian_Antarctic_Expedition">Belgian Antarctic Expedition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roald_Amundsen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Belgian Antarctic Expedition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Belgica_schiff.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="282" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Belgica_schiff.jpg/220px-Belgica_schiff.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Belgica_schiff.jpg/330px-Belgica_schiff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/80/Belgica_schiff.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Belgica_schiff.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/RV_Belgica_(1884)" title="RV Belgica (1884)">RVÂ <i>Belgica</i></a> frozen in the ice, 1898</div></div></div>
<p>Amundsen joined the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Antarctic_Expedition" title="Belgian Antarctic Expedition">Belgian Antarctic Expedition</a> as first mate at the age of 25 in 1897. This expedition, led by <a href="/wiki/Adrien_de_Gerlache" title="Adrien de Gerlache">Adrien de Gerlache</a> using the ship the RV <i>Belgica</i>, became the first expedition to overwinter in Antarctica.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mifflin_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mifflin-8">[8]</a></sup> The <i>Belgica</i>, whether by mistake or design, became locked in the sea ice at 70Â°30â²S off <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Island" title="Alexander Island">Alexander Island</a>, west of the <a href="/wiki/Antarctic_Peninsula" title="Antarctic Peninsula">Antarctic Peninsula</a>. The crew endured a winter for which they were poorly prepared.
</p><p>By Amundsen's own estimation, the doctor for the expedition, the American <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Cook" title="Frederick Cook">Frederick Cook</a>, probably saved the crew from <a href="/wiki/Scurvy" title="Scurvy">scurvy</a> by hunting for animals and feeding the crew fresh meat. In cases where citrus fruits are lacking, uncooked meat â particularly <a href="/wiki/Offal" title="Offal">offal</a> â from animals often contain enough of the vitamin to prevent scurvy and even partly treat it. This was an important lesson for Amundsen's future expeditions. Amundsen and Cook later took over command of the ship when De Gerlache became severely ill.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Northwest_Passage">The Northwest Passage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roald_Amundsen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: The Northwest Passage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nlc_amundsen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="622" data-file-width="443" decoding="async" height="309" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Nlc_amundsen.jpg/220px-Nlc_amundsen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Nlc_amundsen.jpg/330px-Nlc_amundsen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Nlc_amundsen.jpg/440px-Nlc_amundsen.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nlc_amundsen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Amundsen c. 1908</div></div></div>
<p>In 1903, Amundsen led the first expedition to successfully traverse Canada's <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Passage" title="Northwest Passage">Northwest Passage</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific</a> oceans. He planned a small expedition of six men in a <span class="nowrap">45-ton</span> fishing vessel, <a href="/wiki/Gj%C3%B8a" title="GjÃ¸a"><i>GjÃ¸a</i></a>, in order to have flexibility. His ship had relatively shallow draft. His technique was to use a small ship and hug the coast. Amundsen had the ship outfitted with a small 13Â horsepower single-screw paraffin engine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Derry_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Derry-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>They traveled via <a href="/wiki/Baffin_Bay" title="Baffin Bay">Baffin Bay</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Parry_Channel" title="Parry Channel">Parry Channel</a> and then south through <a href="/wiki/Peel_Sound" title="Peel Sound">Peel Sound</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Ross_Strait" title="James Ross Strait">James Ross Strait</a>, <a href="/wiki/Simpson_Strait" title="Simpson Strait">Simpson Strait</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rae_Strait" title="Rae Strait">Rae Strait</a>. They spent two winters at <a href="/wiki/King_William_Island" title="King William Island">King William Island</a>, in the harbor of what is today <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gjoa_Haven,_Nunavut" title="Gjoa Haven, Nunavut">Gjoa Haven</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mifflin_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mifflin-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Derry_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-Derry-9">[9]</a></sup> During this time, Amundsen and the crew learned from the local <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Netsilik_Inuit" title="Netsilik Inuit">Netsilik Inuit</a> about <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a> survival skills, which he found invaluable in his later expedition to the South Pole. For example, he learned to use sled dogs for transportation of goods and to wear animal skins in lieu of heavy, woolen parkas, which could not keep out the cold when wet.
</p><p>Leaving Gjoa Haven, he sailed west and passed <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Bay" title="Cambridge Bay">Cambridge Bay</a>, which had been reached from the west by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Collinson" title="Richard Collinson">Richard Collinson</a> in 1852. Continuing to the south of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Victoria_Island_(Canada)" title="Victoria Island (Canada)">Victoria Island</a>, the ship cleared the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_Arctic_Archipelago" title="Canadian Arctic Archipelago">Canadian Arctic Archipelago</a> on <span class="nowrap">17 August 1905</span>. It had to stop for the winter before going on to <a href="/wiki/Nome,_Alaska" title="Nome, Alaska">Nome</a> on Alaska's Pacific coast. The nearest telegraph station was 500 miles (800Â km) away in <a href="/wiki/Eagle,_Alaska" title="Eagle, Alaska">Eagle</a>. Amundsen traveled there overland to wire a success message on 5 December, then returned to Nome in 1906. Later that year he was elected to the <a href="/wiki/American_Antiquarian_Society" title="American Antiquarian Society">American Antiquarian Society</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p><p>At this time, Amundsen learned of the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_union_between_Norway_and_Sweden" title="Dissolution of the union between Norway and Sweden">dissolution of the union between Norway and Sweden</a>, and that he had a new king. The explorer sent the new king, <a href="/wiki/Haakon_VII_of_Norway" title="Haakon VII of Norway">Haakon VII</a>, news that his traversing the Northwest Passage "was a great achievement for Norway".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-explore_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-explore-11">[11]</a></sup> He said he hoped to do more and signed it "Your loyal subject, Roald Amundsen."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-explore_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-explore-11">[11]</a></sup> The crew returned to Oslo in November 1906, after almost three-and-a-half years abroad. <i>GjÃ¸a</i> was returned to Norway in 1972. After a <span class="nowrap">45-day</span> trip from San Francisco on a bulk carrier, she was placed on land outside the <a href="/wiki/Fram_Museum" title="Fram Museum">Fram Museum</a> in Oslo,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-explore_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-explore-11">[11]</a></sup> where she is now situated inside her own dedicated building at the museum.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Pole_Expedition">South Pole Expedition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roald_Amundsen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: South Pole Expedition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Amundsen%27s_South_Pole_expedition" title="Amundsen's South Pole expedition">Amundsen's South Pole expedition</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aan_de_Zuidpool_-_p1913-160.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="321" data-file-width="486" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Aan_de_Zuidpool_-_p1913-160.jpg/260px-Aan_de_Zuidpool_-_p1913-160.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Aan_de_Zuidpool_-_p1913-160.jpg/390px-Aan_de_Zuidpool_-_p1913-160.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/44/Aan_de_Zuidpool_-_p1913-160.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aan_de_Zuidpool_-_p1913-160.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Norwegian flag at the South Pole</div></div></div>
<p>Amundsen next planned to take an expedition to the North Pole and explore the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Basin" title="Arctic Basin">Arctic Basin</a>. Finding it difficult to raise funds, when he heard in 1909 that the Americans Frederick Cook and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Peary" title="Robert Peary">Robert Peary</a> had claimed to reach the North Pole as a result of two different expeditions, he decided to reroute to Antarctica.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Simpson_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Simpson-12">[12]</a></sup> He was not clear about his intentions, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_F._Scott" title="Robert F. Scott">Robert F. Scott</a> and the Norwegian supporters felt misled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Simpson_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Simpson-12">[12]</a></sup> Scott was planning his own expedition to the South Pole that year. Using the ship <a href="/wiki/Fram_(ship)" title="Fram (ship)"><i>Fram</i></a>, earlier used by <a href="/wiki/Fridtjof_Nansen" title="Fridtjof Nansen">Fridtjof Nansen</a>, Amundsen left Oslo for the south on 3 June 1910.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Simpson_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-Simpson-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Amundsen_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Amundsen-13">[13]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a>, Amundsen alerted his men that they would be heading to Antarctica, and sent a telegram to Scott: "Beg to inform you <i>Fram</i> proceeding Antarctic â Amundsen."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Simpson_12-3"><a href="#cite_note-Simpson-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p><p>Nearly six months later, the expedition arrived at the eastern edge of the <a href="/wiki/Ross_Ice_Shelf" title="Ross Ice Shelf">Ross Ice Shelf</a> (then known as "the Great Ice Barrier"), at a large inlet called the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Whales" title="Bay of Whales">Bay of Whales</a>, on 14 January 1911. Amundsen established his base camp there, calling it <a href="/wiki/Framheim" title="Framheim"><i>Framheim</i></a>. Amundsen eschewed the heavy wool clothing worn on earlier Antarctic attempts in favour of adopting <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a>-style furred skins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thomas_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p><p>Using skis and dog sleds for transportation, Amundsen and his men created supply depots at 80Â°, 81Â° and 82Â°Â South on the Barrier, along a line directly south to the Pole.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thomas_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas-6">[6]</a></sup> Amundsen also planned to kill some of his dogs on the way and use them as a source for fresh meat. As he went he butchered some of the dogs and fed them to the remaining dogs, as well as eating some himself. A small group, including <a href="/wiki/Hjalmar_Johansen" title="Hjalmar Johansen">Hjalmar Johansen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kristian_Prestrud" title="Kristian Prestrud">Kristian Prestrud</a> and <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B8rgen_Stubberud" title="JÃ¸rgen Stubberud">JÃ¸rgen Stubberud</a>, set out on 8 September, but had to abandon their trek due to extreme temperatures. The painful retreat caused a quarrel within the group, and Amundsen sent Johansen and the other two men to explore <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edward_VII_Peninsula" title="Edward VII Peninsula">King Edward VII Land</a>.
</p><p>A second attempt, with a team of five made up of <a href="/wiki/Olav_Bjaaland" title="Olav Bjaaland">Olav Bjaaland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Helmer_Hanssen" title="Helmer Hanssen">Helmer Hanssen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sverre_Hassel" title="Sverre Hassel">Sverre Hassel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Wisting" title="Oscar Wisting">Oscar Wisting</a> and Amundsen, departed base camp on 19 October. They took four sledges and 52Â dogs. Using a route along the previously unknown <a href="/wiki/Axel_Heiberg_Glacier" title="Axel Heiberg Glacier">Axel Heiberg Glacier</a>, they arrived at the edge of the Polar Plateau on 21 November after a four-day climb. The team  and 16Â dogs arrived at the pole on 14 December, a month before Scott's group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[a]</a></sup> Amundsen named their South Pole camp <a href="/wiki/Polheim" title="Polheim">Polheim</a>. Amundsen renamed the <a href="/wiki/Antarctic_Plateau" title="Antarctic Plateau">Antarctic Plateau</a> as King Haakon VII's Plateau. They left a small tent and letter stating their accomplishment, in case they did not return safely to Framheim.
</p><p>The team arrived at Framheim on 25 January 1912, with 11Â surviving dogs. They made their way off the continent and to <a href="/wiki/Hobart" title="Hobart">Hobart</a>, Australia, where Amundsen publicly announced his success on 7 March 1912. He telegraphed news to backers.
</p><p>Amundsen's expedition benefited from his careful preparation, good equipment, appropriate clothing, a simple primary task, an understanding of dogs and their handling, and the effective use of skis. In contrast to the misfortunes of Scott's team, Amundsen's trek proved relatively smooth and uneventful.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Polar_Expeditions_and_The_Northeast_Passage">North Polar Expeditions and The Northeast Passage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roald_Amundsen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: North Polar Expeditions and The Northeast Passage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Northeast_Passage">The Northeast Passage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roald_Amundsen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: The Northeast Passage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Roald_Amundsen&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">April 2021</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Polarskipet_Maud.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="625" decoding="async" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Polarskipet_Maud.jpg/220px-Polarskipet_Maud.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Polarskipet_Maud.jpg/330px-Polarskipet_Maud.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Polarskipet_Maud.jpg/440px-Polarskipet_Maud.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Polarskipet_Maud.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Maud_(ship)" title="Maud (ship)"><i>Maud</i></a> in June 1918</div></div></div>
<p>In 1918, an expedition Amundsen began with a new ship, <a href="/wiki/Maud_(ship)" title="Maud (ship)"><i>Maud</i></a>, lasted until 1925. <i>Maud</i> was carefully navigated through the ice west to east through the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Sea_Route" title="Northern Sea Route">Northeast Passage</a>. With him on this expedition were Oscar Wisting and Helmer Hanssen, both of whom had been part of the team to reach the South Pole. In addition, Henrik LindstrÃ¸m was included as a cook. He suffered a stroke and was so physically reduced that he could not participate.
</p><p>The goal of the expedition was to explore the unknown areas of the Arctic Ocean, strongly inspired by Fridtjof Nansen's earlier expedition with <i>Fram</i>. The plan was to sail along the coast of <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a> and go into the ice farther to the north and east than Nansen had. In contrast to Amundsen's earlier expeditions, this was expected to yield more material for academic research, and he carried the geophysicist <a href="/wiki/Harald_Sverdrup_(oceanographer)" title="Harald Sverdrup (oceanographer)">Harald Sverdrup</a> on board.
</p><p>The voyage was to the northeasterly direction over the <a href="/wiki/Kara_Sea" title="Kara Sea">Kara Sea</a>. Amundsen planned to freeze the <i>Maud</i> into the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_ice_pack" title="Arctic ice pack">polar ice cap</a> and drift towards the North PoleÂ â as Nansen had done with the <i>Fram</i>Â â and he did so off <a href="/wiki/Cape_Chelyuskin" title="Cape Chelyuskin">Cape Chelyuskin</a>. But, the ice became so thick that the ship was unable to break free, although it was designed for such a journey in heavy ice. In September 1919, the crew got the ship loose from the ice, but it froze again after eleven days somewhere between the <a href="/wiki/New_Siberian_Islands" title="New Siberian Islands">New Siberian Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wrangel_Island" title="Wrangel Island">Wrangel Island</a>.
</p><p>During this time, Amundsen suffered a broken arm and was attacked by polar bears.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup> As a result, he participated little in the work outdoors, such as sleigh rides and hunting. He, Hanssen, and Wisting, along with two other men, embarked on an expedition by dog sled to Nome, Alaska, more than 1,000 kilometres (620Â mi) away. But they found that the ice was not frozen solid in the <a href="/wiki/Bering_Strait" title="Bering Strait">Bering Strait</a>, and it could not be crossed. They sent a telegram from <a href="/wiki/Anadyr_(town)" title="Anadyr (town)">Anadyr</a> to signal their location.
</p><p>After two winters frozen in the ice, without having achieved the goal of drifting over the North Pole, Amundsen decided to go to Nome to repair the ship and buy provisions. Several of the crew ashore there, including Hanssen, did not return on time to the ship. Amundsen considered Hanssen to be in breach of contract, and dismissed him from the crew.
</p><p>During the third winter, <i>Maud</i> was frozen in the western Bering Strait. She finally became free and the expedition sailed south, reaching <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>, in the American Pacific Northwest in 1921 for repairs. Amundsen returned to Norway, needing to put his finances in order. He took with him two young indigenous girls, a four-year-old he adopted, Kakonita, and her companion Camilla. When Amundsen went bankrupt two years later, however, he sent the girls to be cared for by Camilla's father, who lived in eastern Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Amundsen_adoption_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Amundsen_adoption-17">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 1922, Amundsen returned to <i>Maud</i>, which had been sailed to Nome.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> He decided to shift from the planned naval expedition to aerial ones, and arranged to charter a plane. He divided the expedition team in two: one part, led by him, was to winter over and prepare for an attempt to fly over the pole in 1923. The second team on <i>Maud</i>, under the command of Wisting, was to resume the original plan to drift over the North Pole in the ice. The ship drifted in the ice for three years east of the New Siberian Islands, never reaching the North Pole. It was finally seized by Amundsen's creditors as  collateral for his mounting debt.
</p><p>Although they were unable to reach the North Pole, the scientific results of the expedition, mainly the work of Sverdrup, have proven to be of considerable value. Much of the carefully collected scientific data was lost during the ill-fated journey of <a href="/wiki/Peter_Tessem_and_Paul_Knutsen" title="Peter Tessem and Paul Knutsen">Peter Tessem and Paul Knutsen</a>, two crew members sent on a mission by Amundsen. The scientific materials were later retrieved by Russian scientist <a href="/wiki/Nikolay_Urvantsev" title="Nikolay Urvantsev">Nikolay Urvantsev</a> from where they had been abandoned on the shores of the <a href="/wiki/Kara_Sea" title="Kara Sea">Kara Sea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barr1919_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barr1919-19">[18]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aerial_Expeditions_to_the_North_Pole">Aerial Expeditions to the North Pole</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roald_Amundsen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Aerial Expeditions to the North Pole">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roald_Amundsen_Svalbard_1925.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="794" data-file-width="1218" decoding="async" height="202" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Roald_Amundsen_Svalbard_1925.jpg/310px-Roald_Amundsen_Svalbard_1925.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Roald_Amundsen_Svalbard_1925.jpg/465px-Roald_Amundsen_Svalbard_1925.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Roald_Amundsen_Svalbard_1925.jpg/620px-Roald_Amundsen_Svalbard_1925.jpg 2x" width="310"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roald_Amundsen_Svalbard_1925.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Amundsen and plane in <a href="/wiki/Svalbard" title="Svalbard">Svalbard</a> (1925)</div></div></div>
<p>The 1923 attempt to fly over the Pole failed. Amundsen and <a href="/wiki/Oskar_Omdal" title="Oskar Omdal">Oskar Omdal</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Norwegian_Navy" title="Royal Norwegian Navy">Royal Norwegian Navy</a>, tried to fly from <a href="/wiki/Wainwright,_Alaska" title="Wainwright, Alaska">Wainwright, Alaska</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Spitsbergen" title="Spitsbergen">Spitsbergen</a> across the North Pole. When their aircraft was damaged, they abandoned the journey. To raise additional funds, Amundsen traveled around the United States in 1924 on a lecture tour.
</p><p>In 1925, accompanied by <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Ellsworth" title="Lincoln Ellsworth">Lincoln Ellsworth</a>, pilot <a href="/wiki/Hjalmar_Riiser-Larsen" title="Hjalmar Riiser-Larsen">Hjalmar Riiser-Larsen</a>, flight mechanic <a href="/wiki/Karl_Feucht" title="Karl Feucht">Karl Feucht</a> and two other team members, Amundsen took two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dornier_Do_J" title="Dornier Do J">Dornier Do J</a> <a href="/wiki/Flying_boat" title="Flying boat">flying boats</a>, the N-24 and N-25, to 87Â°Â 44â²Â north. It was the northernmost latitude reached by plane up to that time. The aircraft landed a few miles apart without radio contact, yet the crews managed to reunite. The N-24 was damaged. Amundsen and his crew worked for more than three weeks to clean up an airstrip to take off from ice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-historynet_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-historynet-20">[19]</a></sup> They shovelled 600 tons of ice while consuming only one pound (400Â g) of daily food rations. In the end, the six crew members were packed into the N-25. In a remarkable feat, Riiser-Larsen took off, and they barely became airborne over the cracking ice. They returned triumphant when everyone thought they had been lost forever.
</p><p>In 1926, Amundsen and 15 other men (including Ellsworth, Riiser-Larsen, Oscar Wisting, and the Italian air crew led by aeronautical engineer <a href="/wiki/Umberto_Nobile" title="Umberto Nobile">Umberto Nobile</a>) made the first crossing of the Arctic in the <a href="/wiki/Airship" title="Airship">airship</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Norge_(airship)" title="Norge (airship)">Norge</a>,</i> designed by Nobile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBSorg_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-PBSorg-21">[20]</a></sup> They left <a href="/wiki/Spitsbergen" title="Spitsbergen">Spitsbergen</a> on 11 May 1926, flew over the North Pole on 12 May,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dailytelegraph_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-dailytelegraph-22">[21]</a></sup> and landed in Alaska the following day.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy_over_Polar_Priority">Controversy over Polar Priority</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roald_Amundsen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Controversy over Polar Priority">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The three previous claims to have arrived at the North Pole: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Cook" title="Frederick Cook">Frederick Cook</a> in 1908; <a href="/wiki/Robert_Peary" title="Robert Peary">Robert Peary</a> in 1909; and <a href="/wiki/Richard_E._Byrd" title="Richard E. Byrd">Richard E. Byrd</a> in 1926 (just a few days before the <i>Norge</i>) are disputed by some, as being either of dubious accuracy or outrightly fraudulent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Henderson2005_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Henderson2005-23">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rawlins2000_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rawlins2000-24">[23]</a></sup> If these other claims are false, the crew of the <i>Norge</i> would be the first explorers verified to have reached the North Pole, when they floated over it in the <i>Norge</i> in 1926.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whowasfirstatthenorthpole_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-whowasfirstatthenorthpole-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dailytelegraph_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-dailytelegraph-22">[21]</a></sup> If the <i>Norge</i> expedition was the first to the North Pole, Amundsen and Oscar Wisting were the first men to have reached both geographical poles, by ground or by air.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Disappearance_and_death">Disappearance and death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roald_Amundsen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Disappearance and death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Latham_47_Roald_Amundsen_1928.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="425" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Latham_47_Roald_Amundsen_1928.jpg/220px-Latham_47_Roald_Amundsen_1928.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Latham_47_Roald_Amundsen_1928.jpg/330px-Latham_47_Roald_Amundsen_1928.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Latham_47_Roald_Amundsen_1928.jpg/440px-Latham_47_Roald_Amundsen_1928.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Latham_47_Roald_Amundsen_1928.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Amundsen's <a href="/wiki/Latham_47" title="Latham 47">Latham 47</a> flying boat</div></div></div>
<p>Amundsen disappeared on 18 June 1928 while flying on a rescue mission in the Arctic. His team included Norwegian pilot <a href="/wiki/Leif_Dietrichson" title="Leif Dietrichson">Leif Dietrichson</a>, French pilot <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Guilbaud" title="RenÃ© Guilbaud">RenÃ© Guilbaud</a>, and three more Frenchmen. They were seeking missing members of Nobile's crew, whose new airship <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Airship_Italia" title="Airship Italia"><i>Italia</i></a> had crashed while returning from the North Pole. Amundsen's French <a href="/wiki/Latham_47" title="Latham 47">Latham 47</a> flying boat <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_aerial_disappearances" title="List of aerial disappearances">never returned</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup>
</p><p>Later, a wing-float and bottom gasoline tank from the plane, which had been adapted as a replacement wing-float, were found near the <a href="/wiki/Troms%C3%B8" title="TromsÃ¸">TromsÃ¸</a> coast. It is assumed that the plane crashed in the <a href="/wiki/Barents_Sea" title="Barents Sea">Barents Sea</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> and that Amundsen and his crew were killed in the wreck, or died shortly afterward. The search for Amundsen and team was called off in September 1928 by the Norwegian government, and the bodies were never found.
</p><p>In 2004 and in late August 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Norwegian_Navy" title="Royal Norwegian Navy">Royal Norwegian Navy</a> used the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AUV" title="AUV">unmanned submarine</a> <i>Hugin 1000</i> to search for the wreckage of Amundsen's plane. The searches focused on a 40-square-mile (100Â km<sup>2</sup>) area of the sea floor, and were documented by the German production company ContextTV.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rincon_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rincon-27">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-searchforamundsen_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-searchforamundsen-28">[27]</a></sup> They found nothing from the Amundsen flight.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roald_Amundsen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Amundsen was a lifelong bachelor, though he had a long-time relationship with the Norwegian-born Kristine Elisabeth ('Kiss') Bennett, the wife of an Englishman, Charles Peto Bennett.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thyvold2012_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thyvold2012-29">[28]</a></sup> He met her in London in 1907 and they remained close for many years, although Amundsen kept the relationship a secret from everyone outside his intimate circle. Later, he became engaged to Bess Magids, an American divorcÃ©e whom he had met in Alaska.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bomann-Larsen2011_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bomann-Larsen2011-30">[29]</a></sup> Though there is little evidence, it was said that Amundsen had a brief affair with his landlady in Antwerp â until he came home and found her dead of an apparent suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> His biographer Tor Bomann-Larsen also suggests a romantic relationship between Amundsen and Sigrid Castberg, wife of the lawyer Leif Castberg from <a href="/wiki/Gj%C3%B8vik" title="GjÃ¸vik">GjÃ¸vik</a>, in the years before the South Pole expedition, a relationship Amundsen broke up after that expedition in favour of Kiss Bennett.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup>
</p><p>Author Julian Sancton noted that in his younger years, Amundsen was said to have ignored romantic relationships in pursuit of his goals. He "found little use in activities that didn't help him fulfill his polar ambitions".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Orders_and_decorations">Orders and decorations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roald_Amundsen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Orders and decorations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="387" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Flag_of_Denmark.svg/20px-Flag_of_Denmark.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Flag_of_Denmark.svg/31px-Flag_of_Denmark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Flag_of_Denmark.svg/40px-Flag_of_Denmark.svg.png 2x" width="20"/>Â </span><a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>:

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roald_Amundsen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_things_named_after_Roald_Amundsen" title="List of things named after Roald Amundsen">List of things named after Roald Amundsen</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Amundsen-scott-south_pole_station_2007.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Amundsen-scott-south_pole_station_2007.jpg/220px-Amundsen-scott-south_pole_station_2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Amundsen-scott-south_pole_station_2007.jpg/330px-Amundsen-scott-south_pole_station_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Amundsen-scott-south_pole_station_2007.jpg/440px-Amundsen-scott-south_pole_station_2007.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Amundsen-scott-south_pole_station_2007.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Amundsen%E2%80%93Scott_South_Pole_Station" title="AmundsenâScott South Pole Station">AmundsenâScott South Pole Station</a></div></div></div>
<p>Owing to Amundsen's numerous significant accomplishments in polar exploration, many places in both the Arctic and Antarctic are named after him. The <a href="/wiki/Amundsen%E2%80%93Scott_South_Pole_Station" title="AmundsenâScott South Pole Station">AmundsenâScott South Pole Station</a>, operated by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Antarctic_Program" title="United States Antarctic Program">United States Antarctic Program</a>, was jointly named in honour of Amundsen and his British rival <a href="/wiki/Robert_Falcon_Scott" title="Robert Falcon Scott">Robert Falcon Scott</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup>
</p><p>The 1969 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Red_Tent_(film)" title="The Red Tent (film)">The Red Tent</a></i> tells the story of the Nobile expedition and Amundsen's disappearance. <a href="/wiki/Sean_Connery" title="Sean Connery">Sean Connery</a> plays the role of Amundsen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup>
</p><p>Huntford's book was adapted into the TV serial <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_Place_on_Earth" title="The Last Place on Earth">The Last Place on Earth</a></i>. It aired in 1985 and featured <a href="/wiki/Sverre_Anker_Ousdal" title="Sverre Anker Ousdal">Sverre Anker Ousdal</a> as Amundsen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 15 February 2019, a biographic Norwegian film titled <i><a href="/wiki/Amundsen_(film)" title="Amundsen (film)">Amundsen</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Espen_Sandberg" title="Espen Sandberg">Espen Sandberg</a>, was released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="European-Inuit_descendant_claims">European-Inuit descendant claims</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roald_Amundsen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: European-Inuit descendant claims">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Roald_Amundsen&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br/><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>Â <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Roald+Amundsen%22" rel="nofollow">"Roald Amundsen"</a>Â âÂ <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Roald+Amundsen%22+-wikipedia&amp;tbs=ar:1" rel="nofollow">news</a>Â <b>Â·</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Roald+Amundsen%22&amp;tbs=bkt:s&amp;tbm=bks" rel="nofollow">newspapers</a>Â <b>Â·</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Roald+Amundsen%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">books</a>Â <b>Â·</b> <a class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Roald+Amundsen%22" rel="nofollow">scholar</a>Â <b>Â·</b> <a class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Roald+Amundsen%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on" rel="nofollow">JSTOR</a></span></small></span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">April 2021</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>At least two Inuit in GjÃ¸a Haven with European ancestry have claimed to be descendants of Amundsen, from the period of their extended winter stay on King William Island from 1903 to 1905.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[49]</a></sup> Accounts by members of the expedition told of their relations with Inuit women, and historians have speculated that Amundsen might also have taken a partner,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup> although he wrote a warning against this.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fram_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-fram-53">[51]</a></sup>
</p><p>Specifically, half-brothers Bob Konona and Paul Ikuallaq say that their father Luke Ikuallaq told them on his deathbed that he was the son of Amundsen. Konona said that their father Ikuallaq was left out on the ice to die after his birth, as his European ancestry made him illegitimate to the Inuit, threatening their community. His Inuit grandparents saved him.
</p><p>In 2012, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Y-DNA" title="Y-DNA">Y-DNA</a> analysis, with the families' permission, showed that Ikuallaq was not a match to the direct male line of Amundsen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fram_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-fram-53">[51]</a></sup> Not all descendants claiming European ancestry have been tested for a match to Amundsen, nor has there been a comparison of Ikuallaq's DNA to that of other European members of Amundsen's crew.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fram_53-2"><a href="#cite_note-fram-53">[51]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roald_Amundsen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roald_Amundsen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"> Some sources give the date as 15 December. <i>Fram</i> crossed the <a href="/wiki/International_Date_Line" title="International Date Line">International Date Line</a> shortly before arriving at the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Whales" title="Bay of Whales">Bay of Whales</a>, and thereby "lost" a day. Since the western and eastern hemispheres are conjoined at the South Pole, either date can be considered as correct, though Amundsen gives 14 December, both in his first telegraphed report on arrival in Hobart, and in his fuller account <i>The South Pole</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAmundsenVol._I,_p._xvii_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAmundsenVol._I,_p._xvii-14">[14]</a></sup> </span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-40"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-40">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Returned on 24 October 1917 in protest of Germany's unrestricted submarine warfare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
